蘇聯與各國的出版品交換工作  王以元　　蘇聯爲要使國内的民衆熟悉國外的工業，農業，科學及文藝等的狀况和獲得更新的一切生產技術，同時把牠自己也介紹給别人，告訴别人牠的社會主義建設與工農的生活，所以有對外文化聯絡會（ＶＯＫＳ）的組織。由這聯絡會每年向外國交換出版物，招待各國文化界的參觀等，其成績頗爲可驚。牠在交換出版品方面，已和世界上的七十個國家發生關係，其中以法，德，意，比，捷克，匈，挪威，拉特維亞，荷，美等國爲最多。從一九二四到一九三三年經過聯絡會交換的書有一·四二二·八八一册。單在一九三二年有二一六·八一六册分配到蘇聯以下各邦：俄羅斯本部　一四九·一八○册烏克蘭，二九·○七六册白俄羅斯　一五·二八八册喬奇亞　六·一三五册亞美尼亞　三三三册亞熱爾拜然　一·四九○册烏茲白克斯坦　一二·二二四册土克門尼斯坦　三·○九○册總計　二一六·八一六册　　通過聯絡會來的社團交換出版品的信，是年有增加，如下表：一九二五年　　一一八一九二六年　四○六一九二七年　一·四八四一九二八年　二·三四九一九二九年　三·○七二一九三○年　三·四六九一九三一年　三·七五○一九三二年　四·○六○一九三三年（一月一日止）　四·三六八　　這些信可分作下面幾類：類别　國内件數　國外件數學院　一三　八五研究所及實騐所　四三七一·一九二科學社　一二九　五四六大學及高級學校　七四　三四九政府辦公處及公共圖書館　一八五　一九一博物院　七○　一二七科學雜誌編輯部　二四五　五四六個人的科學工作者　六二　一二一　　下面是一九三二年出版品交換的内容的分類表：類别　從國外來的　從國内寄出％的％文學及傳記　五·一二　三·六五政治，社會學，法律　五·四三　八·九○經濟，財政，交通，統計　一五·七六　二一·○○敎育，敎授法　二·三二　二·七○自然史，普通科學　二一·二二　一○·四五技術　四·九七　三一·○○農業，家畜董療學　二五·二二　一四·一○歷史，人類學　四·三八　二·五三其他　一五·五四　五·七四文藝作品作文品藝榮興米行  嚴白壁　　是一九ＸＸ年的春季。出名「　小二伯伯」的岳卿先生，突然在Ｘ鎭北市獨資開設了一爿榮興米行。　　岳卿先生雖然沒有學過生意，但他的理財手段却很精明。從一個苦秀才出身，坐過私塾，開過靑葉行，當過學務委員，做過縣議員，平時做着絲綢的抵押和買賣，所以也多了些錢，造起四開間門面的兩埭樓房，買進一百多畝田地·似乎已是小康之家了。　　他很不容易的撑起這份家產，但他還不能就此休息，他的家庭的干金擔的重負，還壓在他的肩膀上。他有七十餘歲的老父老母，五十餘歲的妻子，二十餘歲的兩個兒子：——大的一個失了業，在家坐吃；小的一個在縣城裏當小學敎員，出息很少。——都娶着媳婦，而且都已有了子女。　　他有這份家產，苦飯當然可以敷衍了。但他是一個感覺靈敏的人，當革命勢力到達Ｘ鎭後，他就料到田產是不可靠了，所以情願賤一點賣掉。他又覺到長袍知褂的紳士會在這個年頭吃了虧，所以他就做了一套中山裝。雖然時過境遷，形式上長袍短褂未必吃了虧，但他終覺得舊秩序已變了個花樣。在這樣的花樣裏，他預感未來生活的恐慌。他時常敎訓兩個兒子，要開源節流。節流方面，他在「自奉」上，早已做到了，開源方面，他想創立一個商業基礎，使兒子們只要能够守成，就不愁沒飯吃。他幾次的思慮，决定開設一爿米行，因爲他看到上一年的下半年的米價，是在步步高漲的過程中。　　他在Ｘ鎭上也是一個有權力的人物，四鄕農民都很敬重他，都呌他「二先生」。他有着開靑葉行的商業經騐。這此，促成他深深的自信。　　當漆得很漂亮的「官牙榮興米行」招牌還放着在漆店裏的時候，他曾經很得意的在金家茶館裏宜佈過他的「大政方針」，說要呌大兒子學「武塲」，自己坐賬房，將來營業發達了，再呌小兒子來替手，他自己就可以單「坐高凳」了！　　榮興米行正式開張了。四鄕農民都爭先恐後的去賒米吃，借錢用。對付這種「信用」的交易，岳卿先生用的是保證手續，就是每鄕要賒米借錢的人，必須邀到「船家長」。但農民們大半都認識岳卿先生的，「二先生」，「二先生」，呌得很親熱，所以有些竟運這些手續也免除了的。　　光陰飛快的過去，蠶汛罷了，欠賬的農民賣了繭回來，都一五一十的到榮與米行裏來還賬。　　岳卿先一坐在賬桌旁，翻開賬簿，撥動算珠，咪花眼笑的從農民手中接受洋鈿。本利還淸了，農民又翻了幾袋米去。這樣𢌞環往復，統計起來，大約有四五百次。　　另一面，報米價的市信上，天天有「存底不豐」的字樣，於是他向上海進了一批「小絞米」。　　不久，米價果然高漲了，縱十四幾角一直漲到十九元有零。榮興米行掛牌「拚小绞」現價是十七元五角，賒價是十八元不加利。　　岳卿先生眼看着賬簿上的盈餘數一天天的上升，他樂極啦，但也辛苦極啦！因此，他寫了封信給他的小兒子琤君，呌他立刻辭職返里，帮助管理行務。　　下兩天，榮興米行的賬房，便改由琤君坐了。　　琤君是服務敎育界的人，商情完全是外行，農民又不熟識，所以只有機械的做些「寫」，「算」，「收」，「付」的工作。　　岳卿先生自從有了小兒子替力以後，他自由得多了。空閒的時候，時常跑到附近的鄕下去，觀察農家的情形。這時風調雨順，苗秀葉靑，眼看是一個豐年。缺米的恐慌消滅了，米價便漸跌進「退潮」裏去了。每石初由十九元跌到十八元，岳卿先生還坦然自若，農民也還不知不覺。後來繼續跌下去到十六元，更由十六元跌至十四元，跌勢如排山倒海，更後來竟跌近十二元。農村裏泛起一片嘆聲。　　「糟了！」岳卿先生發着抖。　　「怎麽了呢！」岳卿先生慌張了！　　但還留着一線希望，就是敎望田稻豐收，米價不再跌，心想農民還可拿一石五斗的新米來還一石「拼小絞」的賒米。　　一天天過去，田稻試花了，岳卿先生大淸早便到鄕下去看稻，從那天起，他天天去看，似乎已看上了癮。　　「還好，沒有毛病。」他略略寛了心。　　不料在中秋後一天的夜裏，漫天括了一次大風，吹得岳卿先生的住身房子有些動盪。　　「不好了！」他突然從床上跳了起來。他的一家老小都在夢中，給他這一聲大呌嚇醒了，都披衣起來趕到他的房間裏。只見他僅僅穿着一身單布衫褲，呆呆地立在床邊。他的老父老母問他，他不回答，他的妻子問他，他也不回答，他的兒子媳婦問他，他依然沒有回答。　　「吃官司！」隔了一回，他大呌一聲，跳進床裏去睡了。各人的心頭都覺到他是「瘋了」！但都藴藏着沒有勇氣說出口來。　　等到岳卿先生完全睡熟後，他的母，妻，和兩個媳婦，才輕聲地計議着祈禳。他的小兒子琤君却在憂慮着行務，深恐這種消息傳出去，會影響到一切。他的大兒子遊君却還未理解到這些未來的危機。　　從這夜起，本來很拘謹的岳卿先生一變而爲極落拓了，琤君恐怕他父親在外面「露形」，所以隨時跟着。　　新米上市了，洋米大批進口了！米價又大跌特跌，先跌破十元大關，後來更跌到九元。本地又受了風災，收成減色，到處都聽得到農民的嘆息。岳卿先生的舉動也　外異樣了　　一天早上，他立在門口，琤君緊跟着。他把眼鏡除下，琤君以爲他要措刷，不能爲奇。不料岳卿先生却把眼鏡向階沿石上一摔，恨恨的說一聲「我不要你了！」轉身就向屋裏跑，琤君要想搶住眼鏡已來不及，要拖住父親，又來不及，心裏發了慌，茫茫然向父親的背影追去。　　另一天晚上，他聽到門外一陣急劇的脚步聲，他就亂嚷來了！」「來了！」一溜渐跑上樓，從樓窗爬出去，一直爬上屋頂。他在上面像在平地一般的逃跑着，幸虧琤君敏捷，上屋去抱住父親，再呌幾個人上去，才扶得他平安下來。　　岳卿先生這兩次驚人的舉動，說明了他半個月不到金家茶館吃茶的原因。每個茶客的心頭，都出乎意外的跳動一下。　　後來他的家人給他送到縣城Ｘ醫院去醫治，但毫無效騐，所以住上半個月，便回來了。　　回來後，琤君看到新米汛快要過了，忙着支配他的哥哥帶領行友到鄕下去收賬，一面隨時把收進的欵項，化零爲整，去還到期存欵和介莊欵。　　家裏的女人們，一面忙着許願祈禳問卜，一面輪流着留心岳卿先生的意外。　　但是岳卿先生呢？他却趁家人一個疏忽，關起房門，用一根繩子，在床上做一個結，把自己蓬鬆的留有髭鬚的頭　了進去。常識職業生活與精神衛生  普醫　　據專家調查，精神上的疾病通常要比身體上的疾病來得多些。這只要看自殺，瘋狂，神經衰弱，憂鬱症，女子的歇斯特里亞·····的普遍的流行，已可見其端倪。平常我們總以爲患精神病（廣義的）者少：實際乃是社會上只有身體病患者的醫院，而缺乏精神病患者的醫院，所以才顯得少；而初期的精神病患者，又因爲自己的無知，沒有向醫生——當然很少治療精神病的醫生——求治，其病象不願罷了。我們可以說，在近代的文明世界中，幾乎人人有患精神病的傾向的。尤其在經濟恐慌深刻化，就業困難的今日中國社會裏，精神上的不健康，將是一個普遍而嚴重的現象。中國的失業者不用說，他們已用憂鬱，自殺，瘋狂·····說明他們對於環境適應之悲慘的失敗了；在業者，除了少數環境好的幸運兒外，他們亦正是或多或少地受着這殘酷的病魔的磨折。有多少人能够逃過這可怕的「文明病」的襲擊呢？　　在這裏，有幾種理由，使我要向現在的就業者，說明他們應注意這一事態發展的必要。他們是很容易成爲精神不健康的患者的。　　第一，多數就業者的年齡，中年壯年者最多，而這年齡又適係最易罹此病的年齡。通常人在三十至四十的時期中言論中國未來的危機與出路  亞靈　　中國未來的運命，大槪總是凶多吉少的。如果我們不趕快覺悟振作起來，這一塊豐美的土地，卽使不至整個被一二人所獨佔，也要零碎的給多數人所分割。中國本是一隻紙老虎，自從這紙老虎被人撕破，許多野心家都觸動了覬觎之念。於是瓜分共管的聲浪，便時常刺入我們的耳朶。只因列强勢均力敵，這個要爭肥，那個想掠美，分割難平，未施毒手，使我們至今得以僥倖苟延殘喘。當此之際，倘我國能淸醒猛悟，乘敵人對峙局勢，銳意奮勉自强，以冀得由敵人力爼下解脫出來，國家前途，或有一轉機的希望。但我國民族，目光短小，凡事只求偷安一時，不作向上發展的努力，致國家元氣，日漸衰弱，國際地位，日見低降，終未能打破列强瓜分共管的迷夢。　　我國旣置身列强環同之中，有識者早知其難以相安久處。曾幾何時，一聲霹靂，日人鐵蹄，竟長驅直入，伸進我東北國土，開始其蹂躪我國的步伐。事過兩年有餘，我國方喘息未定，敵人今且作更進一層的策劃，突然向世界致一聲明書，以門羅主義招牌昭示各國，陰謀擯絶列强勢力於東亞之外，挾迫我國於其統轄之下，以遂其獨覇東亞的野心。　敗後的我國，受此打擊，豈不岌岌可危？　　日本聲明書發出後，舉世騷然。各國當局，對此十分重視，皆憤暴日此種行爲，無異向世界挑單，預料太平洋局面，已轉入一新階段，相率起而與之對抗。輿論界的激烈攻擊，尤見怒形於色。英國已有引用九國公約以制日本的意向。國聯亦有拉攏美俄以挫日本的趨勢。行見事態的擴展，將越發嚴重，而演成二次大戰的慘劇。　　世界危機，已急轉直下了，今後我國將何以應此大難？獨力對付强日，當無此把握，亦無此勇氣。那末另一路徑，只有結合列强，和列强取一致行動，以與日本相周旋了。但是列强果能靠得住嗎？須知國際關係，純以利害爲轉移，根本沒有什麽道義存於其間。列强此次對日的反響，目的並不是想援助我國，百是要和日本爭奪遠東市塲。看他們所斤斤計較的，多在一些什麽門户開放機會均等等上面用工夫，何曾有保全我國主權和領土的好意。明白地說，卽是要和日本分沾。利益。我們只要把美記者向齋藤詢問日本是否願意與世界合作共管中國一語細加吟味，便不難揣測出列强的居心所在了。倘日本此刻能放棄其獨覇東亞的私心，誠意和列强勾結，以瓜分或共管中國，我們敢斷言，列强無不表示贊同的。　　因此，我們以爲中國將來卽下被日本獨佔，做日本的附庸，亦必給列强共管，做列强的隸屬。故我國今後的出路，唯有充實自己的力量，作最後的苦鬥，從死裏去求生存。若希冀苟安，倚賴他人，則其結果必至滅亡也無疑！

1934.04.29

Hirota's Reply to British and American Ambassadors: Intention to Withdraw Declaration Regarding China; Attempted Exploration Fails, Corrective Document Issued; Britain and America Satisfied, Consider the Incident Concluded 1

(Tokyo) Japan is now retracting its position stated in the policy statement on China of April 17th. It is unknown whether Japan did this because this astonishing statement caused repercussions around the world. Foreign Minister Hirota now believes that the statement of April 17th did not "formally exist". The statement was issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and was of an informal nature. Hirota has notified the diplomatic community of this and stated that Japan's policy regarding the Far East can be summarized by the second statement issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokesman on April 20: "We desire the unity and prosperity of China, knowing that Japan, due to its geographical location, can gain additional benefits if China is unified and prosperous. However, China's unity and prosperity must come from China's own awareness and efforts." It is reported that the Japanese government has replied in writing to the British and American ambassadors to Japan on Thursday night in accordance with this intention. As for the words in the second statement by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs spokesman on April 20, "It cannot be obtained by other powers claiming development, but it must be known that the era in which other powers or the League of Nations used their power to take advantage of China for their own benefit is now over," which were not included in the written reply to China on Thursday night, it seems that they no longer summarize Japan's policy. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(London) Since Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota explained the declaration regarding China to British Ambassador to Japan, Lindley, the British government now considers the incident to be over. Officials formally stated to the press this afternoon that Foreign Secretary Simon will announce in the House of Commons on Monday that the government considers this to be "much ado about nothing" and is completely satisfied with and accepts Foreign Minister Hirota's explanation regarding the statement of April 17. Diplomatic circles believe that the American government shares the same view as Britain on this matter. According to a semi-official source here, "After Foreign Secretary Simon makes a statement in the House of Commons on Monday, there will be no further action." (Kokumin dispatch, 28th)

Tokyo Announces the Content of Anglo-Japanese Negotiations; Hirota Appeals to the Conscience of All Nations; British Ambassador Retires and Returns Home Yesterday 2

(Tokyo) British Foreign Secretary Simon, fearing that the British Parliament currently in session would inquire about the true meaning of the so-called informal statement of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, ordered Ambassador to Japan Lindley to visit Foreign Minister Hirota to prepare for a response in Parliament. All details have been reported in previous dispatches. Foreign Secretary Simon will report the content of Ambassador Lindley's meeting with Foreign Minister Hirota to Parliament, and Tokyo will also announce it at the same time in order to dispel misunderstandings from Britain, America, and other countries around the world. The content of the meeting is generally as follows:

Questions from Ambassador Lindley 3

(1) What is Japan's view on the application of the Nine-Power Treaty to China? (2) Does Japan maintain the Open Door Policy and the principle of equal opportunity in China? (3) Does Japan intend to hinder other countries' trade with China? (4) Japan claims that the supply of weapons to China by various countries is disturbing peace in East Asia. Which country is Japan considering to be disrupting order in China? Foreign Minister Hirota's response: The words of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs authorities were informal, and it was unexpected that they would attract the attention of Britain. I now answer the questions. (1) Japan maintains the Nine-Power Treaty on China, which has not changed in the past or present, and has no intention of violating the treaty. (2) The same applies to the Open Door Policy. Japan also hopes for the opening of China's door. (3) There is no intention to hinder other countries' fair trade with China. (4) It is difficult to answer which country is considered to be disrupting order in China. One can only ask the conscience of those currently supplying weapons to China. Japan cannot stand idly by when a fire is started in its neighbor's house.

Furthermore, on the evening of the 26th, the main points of the English translation of the statement were conveyed to British Ambassador Lindley and American Ambassador Grew by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the content of the meeting was also published. (Dentsu dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) British Ambassador to Japan, Lindley, retired because of old age and left from Tokyo Station at 1:40 PM on the 28th. Executives of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and many others went to the station together to see him off. The ambassador is scheduled to take the Queen of Asia from Yokohama at 3:00 PM today and will return home via Canada. Before the successor ambassador arrives, it is said that Counselor Tredennick will temporarily take over his duties. (Nichiren dispatch, 28th)

(London) It is reported that Foreign Secretary Simon will elaborate on Japan's declaration of "No encroachment on China" in the House of Commons on Monday and will submit to the House the telegram reporting British Ambassador to Tokyo Lindley's conversation with Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota. He will also present a document given to him by Foreign Minister Hirota a few hours after Ambassador Lindley and Ambassador Grew received the official Japanese declaration on the matter. The official Japanese declaration to the United States has several points that differ from the original declaration made by the spokesman of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. There are currently no signs in London that the British government will take further action on this case. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Main Points of Hirota's Document as Reported by the Japanese News Agency: Contacted Director of Information, Amau; Created Official Translation Delivered to US Ambassador 4

(Tokyo) Regarding the issue of Japan's unofficial statement, American Ambassador Grew previously visited Foreign Minister Hirota, requesting the official English translation of this unofficial statement. Foreign Minister Hirota replied that this was an informal conversation and would contact Director of Information Amau to create an official translation. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent this translation to the US Embassy yesterday. (Dentsu dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) When U.S. Ambassador to Japan Grew visited Foreign Minister Hirota on the 26th, he requested an English translation of the statement on China policy recently issued by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs. As a result of consultations between the Foreign Minister and his leadership, the contents of the statement were explained in English in great detail and a document was created. At 6 p.m. officials were sent to the U.S. Embassy to hand it to the Ambassador. The main parts of its content are as follows:

(1) Japan is the stabilizing force of East Asian peace and bears the full responsibility for maintaining East Asian peace. This unofficial statement is nothing more than a declaration of the Japanese government's policy to the world.

(2) If China achieves its goals of unity and prosperity, Japan will also benefit due to its geographical relationship. Therefore, the Japanese government has no intention of interfering with China's right to independence. However, China's unity requires China's own awakening and efforts, and it can never be achieved by other countries seizing benefits for themselves.

(3) The Japanese government has no intention of interfering with the rights and interests of third countries in China. If third countries engage in commerce and trade with China, mainly for the benefit of the Chinese people, the Japanese government welcomes such activities by third countries.

(4) The Japanese government has no intention of violating the Open Door Policy and the principle of equal opportunity in China, or existing treaties.

(5) However, if the Japanese government sees third countries taking actions that disrupt East Asian peace and order, it will resolutely oppose them, regardless of their form or reason.

(6) The Japanese government hopes that various countries will recognize the fair and free actions of "Manchukuo," but Japan has no territorial ambitions for "Manchukuo."

(7) In short, Japan and other Asian countries, especially China, share the responsibility for maintaining peace in East Asia. (Nichiren dispatch, 28th)

Ariyoshi Meets with Hirota, Denies Military Assistance from Various Countries; Calls for Japanese Not to Be Overly Sensitive 5

(Tokyo) Ariyoshi Akira, the Japanese minister to China, returned to Tokyo today and went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 1:40 PM to meet with Foreign Minister Hirota to report on his return and all circumstances. (Nichiren dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) After meeting with Foreign Minister Hirota this afternoon, Minister Ariyoshi made the following remarks to reporters: There is no important matter for this return. The Nanchang Conference is also a routine matter and does not have the nature of a conference. The League of Nations' aid to China is actually under investigation and has not yet materialized. How the League of Nations wants to do it is quite good. However, because Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, international capital loans to China through the League of Nations will become an international joint management of China excluding Japan, so it is absolutely opposed. If the various countries provide separate and legitimate assistance for industrial development, it is not a problem. As for the supply of weapons, since Chiang Kai-shek is suppressing the communists, weapons may also be necessary. Other economic and military assistance from the various countries are only rumors, and although there may be some truth to them, one should not be overly sensitive. In short, it can be asserted that Sino-Japanese relations will improve. (Dentsu dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) Japanese Minister to China Ariyoshi Akira and his party arrived at Tokyo Station at 9:00 AM this morning. Minister Ariyoshi told reporters that recently foreign countries have gradually understood Japan's fundamental spirit in East Asia. I believe that Sino-Japanese relations are better than last year. The problem of the country of origin marking regulations has been satisfactorily resolved, and other pending Sino-Japanese issues are gradually being resolved. Therefore, now is not the time to initiate concrete negotiations. The Japanese government and public attach great importance to the Nanchang Conference, but in fact the meeting is not of great importance. It is just Huang Fu going south to meet with Wang Jingwei and Chiang Kai-shek. Various pending issues in North China are currently being resolved. The so-called traffic issue is just a matter of changing trains. Postal services between China and "Manchukuo" have in fact been implemented, but because "Manchukuo" is not recognized, supplementary fees are charged. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' statement on China policy has caused a stir in various circles. Among the League of Nations' technical cooperation with China, nothing is currently being implemented. Japan has no intention of interfering with foreign aid to China, but if the aid takes a wrong step, it will lead to the problem of international management of China. However, various countries are forced to implement legitimate development projects separately. As for the purchase of military supplies, because it is the life and death problem of the Chinese government to suppress the Red Army, it is necessary to purchase the necessary weapons from foreign countries. Japan does not need to be overly sensitive about China's purchase of military supplies. In short, Sino-Japanese relations have yielded considerable results under the understanding of the two countries. I hope to promote its concretization through direct negotiations (which have already begun). (Nichiren dispatch, 28th)

British Trades Union Congress: Strongly Advocates Russian Admission to the League of Nations to Counteract Japanese Threats 9

The above resolution of the Trades Union Congress has attracted great attention in Geneva. This is generally believed here. U.S. Navy Reunion Asks for Funds to Implement Shipbuilding Program; Mere Gestures Are Meaningless; Now Is the Time to Expand the Navy 10

(Washington) The U.S. Navy Reunion issued a declaration today, stating that if funds cannot be allocated to continue the shipbuilding program stipulated in the Vinson-Trammell Act for a superior navy, the U.S. Navy will fall to third place. The Navy Reunion solemnly stated that although the Vinson-Trammell plan has been passed by Congress and signed by the President, these gestures are meaningless unless they are supported by funds to build the 102 battleships and 1,184 naval aircraft permitted by the plan. The declaration also requested Congress to pass a budget allocation bill to subsidize the plan. The declaration concluded by saying that now is the time to bring the U.S. Navy to the limits allowed by the treaty. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(Washington) The United States seems to be waiting for detailed reports from the British and American ambassadors to Japan before taking concrete action against Japan. Officials claim that all countries related to the Far East should participate in this preliminary meeting. The actions of Japan that exceed the treaty should be strictly corrected. China, as a signatory to the Nine-Power Treaty and a member of the League of Nations, and also insulted by the Japanese side, should open up a path in this and use the international sacred treaty to seriously correct and restrain this expression from the Japanese side. Regarding this point, it is the unanimous opinion of the various committees. After the review is finalized and submitted to the general meeting for discussion, it will be sent to the central government for suggestions and handed over to the diplomatic authorities for reference. New York Times Editorial: Signatories to the China Treaty Should Respect the Dignity of the Treaty 13

(Nanjing) Washington, 26th - The New York Times editorial stated that President Roosevelt instructed the U.S. State Department yesterday to narrate a summary of the privileges and obligations under the Nine-Power Treaty. This fact is extremely simple. According to the Nine-Power Treaty, in addition to agreeing to respect the sovereignty, independence, and territorial and administrative integrity of China, the various countries also agreed never to support their own people in seeking any means to obtain general preferential rights related to commercial or economic development in any designated area in China. Although the Japanese side claims that it has no intention of violating the regulations and reserves the right to interpret them, according to the Japanese statement, it is clearly in violation of the treaty. According to the opinion of the editorial writer, according to Article 7 of the Nine-Power Treaty, apart from China and Japan, Britain and other signatory countries should have joint diplomatic action. From the perspective of London and Washington, doing so is not only for the benefit of their countries, but also to respect the solemn treaty that is still in effect. If Britain, the United States, and other signatory countries do not consult with each other regarding Japan's clear violation of the treaty, then those countries themselves cannot avoid the suspicion of violating the treaty. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Current Affairs Commentary

Has Japan's Position Really Been Cancelled? 17

Yesterday's Reuters Tokyo dispatch stated, "Japan is now retracting its position stated in the policy statement on China of April 17th." "Foreign Minister Hirota now believes that the statement of April 17th did not formally exist," and so on. At first glance, it seems as if Japan is indeed showing signs of softening due to the strong pressure of world public opinion. In reality, under the control of warlord forces, the Tokyo government would not dare to directly and readily admit defeat without suffering a serious material blow. Furthermore, considering the long-standing and calculating nature of Japanese diplomacy and the significance of the content of the April 17th statement, it can be asserted that the issuance of the statement was by no means a hasty and ill-considered action. It is safe to say that the international reaction was already anticipated by the Japanese, and their plan to respond to it must have been carefully planned. Therefore, the claim of canceling the position should be seen as a predetermined step by the Japanese, rather than a sign of Japanese softening. Knowing this, we should not only not be complacent about it, but also take it as a profound warning. The Japanese have been plotting against us with great care for decades. Whenever their policy towards China seems relaxed, it is when they are actively preparing their invasion plans. They are good at playing the game of feigning retreat to advance.

Now, try asking anyone who knows the situation in the Far East, "Is Japan really willing to repent, change its course, and interact with China in the spirit of genuine friendship?" The answer will undoubtedly be "no." Therefore, the claim that Foreign Minister Hirota's recent statement of canceling the position can erase the marks that have been clearly etched in the minds of the world these past ten days or so, who would believe it? It is precisely because these marks cannot be easily erased that the initial mission of issuing the statement can be considered achieved. The target of the statement is to oppose all international aid to China in terms of technology or finance. Its form of creating enemies is multifaceted. However, it is unlikely that the Japanese will rely on their existing strength to take a further step and directly exert pressure on all sides. No one in their right mind would want to engage in hand-to-hand combat everywhere and put themselves in a position of certain defeat. Moreover, the cunning Japanese would never do this. From this, it can be inferred that even if the League of Nations continues to conduct technical cooperation with China, the Japanese can only exert limited direct pressure on the League of Nations. If that is the case with the League of Nations, which has no military force, it goes without saying for Britain and the United States, which possess powerful military forces. To give one example, Japan's opposition to the import of American aircraft into China is permissible in mere words. However, if they were to directly block Chinese ports with warships, preventing imports, or even intercepting them halfway and forcibly extracting them, it would inevitably lead to war. This is something the Japanese would not want to rashly engage in. Therefore, the statement of April 17th is nothing more than an attempt to make the League of Nations, Britain, the United States, and other countries add another layer of caution when dealing with matters. At the same time, it is an extremely serious warning to our country. The League of Nations and the United States do not need to fear Japan's direct pressure, but the added concern that comes with it cannot be dispelled by Foreign Minister Hirota's statement of "canceling the position." As for the threat to our country, it has the possibility of being realized at any time. Japan only needs to use indirect means to force our country to close its doors and not interact with the League of Nations, Britain, and the United States, while placing itself in the position of a third party that bears no responsibility. If the European and American powers complain, they should only question China and not involve Japan. This is the necessary strategy for Japan to implement its statement, which will make it impossible for the powers to use treaties to prevent it, and our country will have no way to rely on foreign aid to resist.

From this analysis, it can be seen that Japan's position taken in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' statement on the 17th has its own methods for maintaining and promoting it and will certainly not be canceled. Whether its existence is formal or informal is irrelevant. If our country truly wants to implement the purpose of resisting power, it should embrace the determination of fervent sacrifice, grit our teeth, and strive for the final victory. We must not be excited by Hirota's words today and frustrated by his words tomorrow. Intelligent countries like Britain and the United States should not be deceived by Hirota's smokescreen and adopt a "live and let live" attitude.

Guangchang City Has Been Recovered 18

The Pseudo Ninth Army Corps suffers repeated defeats. The Nanchang Headquarters has just received a telegram from the front lines stating that our troops have recovered Guangchang County this afternoon and are currently annihilating the remaining bandits, issuing proclamations to pacify the people, and beginning relief work. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanchang) Chen Cheng's troops fought fiercely with bandits near Guangchang County, completely eliminating the main force of the pseudo 135th Army Corps. The Guangchang Pagoda is now in sight, and recovery is imminent. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanchang) After the Three Route Army captured Ganzhu, the bandits gathered all their forces densely along the border of Nanfeng and Guangchang. On the 19th, Fan's troops attacked and advanced towards the bandits at Yanfu Ridge. The pseudo Sixth Division stubbornly resisted from their stronghold, but we captured the stronghold and advanced to Tiegukeng. Most of the bandits counterattacked from Mount Daluo. Zhou's division counterattacked the bandits on the 20th, engaging in fierce hand-to-hand combat, killing dozens of pseudo regimental and battalion commanders. Over a thousand bandit corpses were left on the battlefield, and the remaining bandits retreated southeast. At that time, Fan's division encountered the bandits at Guangchang and Raojiapu. Peng Dehuai led the densely packed ranks of the pseudo 13th Army Corps in a fierce assault. Just as Kong's division arrived to join the left flank, the bandits, despite shouting loudly and charging, ultimately failed and suffered thousands of casualties. On the 21st, we pursued south in victory. Huang and Xia's two divisions advanced west along the river. The pseudo Ninth Army Corps was repeatedly attacked, and the pseudo Fourteenth Division Commander Zhang Jiwu was killed. We captured Changsheng Bridge, ten li from Guangchang City. On the same day, Fu's division captured Kuzhukeng, east of Changsheng Bridge, and destroyed many bandit strongholds. Xie and Xiao's two divisions routed the pseudo Fifth Army Corps' 13th and 6th divisions, capturing Gaoduan. From the 19th to the 22nd, the main force of the Guangchang bandits was completely defeated, and the county seat was about to fall. (Special dispatch, 26th/28th)

(Nanchang) A victory telegram from Le'an reports that a certain division captured Zengtian, 20 li south of the city, on the morning of the 22nd, and the bandits retreated to Wangxian. Another telegram from Yongfeng reports that a certain division routed the pseudo 23rd Division at Kukeng, near Shaxi, on the 21st. Another certain division captured Shanggu and is pressing on Ningdu on the 22nd. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Nanchang) A victory telegram from Hekou reports that a certain division attacked Fang Zhimin's band at Neilianhu on the 18th. Just as the pseudo Tenth Army Corps was defeated and returned from northern Fujian, they retreated together to San Da Shi Nei, outside Lianhu. Our division is currently besieging them. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Nanchang) A victory telegram from Nanfeng reports that most of the bandits have retreated to Guangchang City. Our vanguard troops have captured Outang and Yaopaizhou. Guangchang City is expected to fall today or tomorrow. Refugees who have fled Guangchang County are being taken care of. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Hankou) Chen Jicheng's troops routed a bandit independent regiment and a guerrilla unit at Zhengjiagou, south of Nanshi, and destroyed the pseudo armory at Longzishan, seizing many guns and ammunition. The bandits in southern Hubei will be eliminated. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Hankou) Military news reports that the Wang and Ma bandits fled to Suizao. Their main force was defeated by Luo Qijiang's troops. Several hundred mounted bandits fled to Wangjiatai via Ju. A large group of remnant bandits was discovered at Renshi Ji Baisudian in Huangchuan and were suppressed by Wang Yizhe's troops, planning to flee to Shangcheng. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Jiang Dingwen goes to Longyan to supervise the suppression. News from Zhangzhou (Xiamen) states that the bandits who had occupied Yong'an completely withdrew towards Qingliu after the afternoon of the 25th. Our troops are currently in pursuit. Jiang Dingwen went from Zhangzhou to Longyan on the 26th and is stationed in Yan to supervise the troops and command the operations. The Fourth Column in western Fujian is advancing towards Tinglian. Half of the Yutian Militia Disarmed; the Other Half Fled to Malanyu with the Japanese. There are Rumors that Militia Leader Wang Bingxiao is Under Surveillance. 22

(Tianjin) On the 27th, Wei Yonghe, the commander of the Second Brigade of the War Zone Security Force, led his troops to Mashan Bridge and surrounded and disarmed 160 members of the rebelling Yutian militia. The remaining 150 members fled to Malage, guided by Japanese ronin. Wei inquired by phone with the Japanese garrison commander in the area whether they intended to lead the rebel unit across the Great Wall line into the puppet territory. The Japanese side replied that they would absolutely not allow it. The whereabouts of Wang Bingkao, the leader of the Yutian militia, are unknown. It is rumored that he is under surveillance by Wei Yonghe's troops, but officials have not confirmed this. It is reported that the rebellion was due to Wang's lack of command ability. His subordinates did not want to disband and, after being incited by Japanese ronin, supported Wang in rebelling, intending to join the puppet state. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng paid a visit to Yu Xuezhong this morning. After returning, he immediately used a long-distance telephone to instruct Wei Yonghe to be responsible for preventing the militia from fleeing abroad. The Yutian security team originally had a feud with the militia, but is taking a calm approach to the matter. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Official sources say that Wang Bingxiao's militia was recruited and trained by himself and was not approved by the provincial government. Wang had served as the Yutian security chief two years ago and was divided into two factions with the local gentry. When Hu took over Wang's troops, the two sides were quite at odds. Wang then recruited the militia for self-defense, and the funds were all from his private wealth. The battle at Yanhong Bridge two months ago was a conflict between Wang and Hu's troops. Later, they were defeated and retreated outside the city to Tuanshanzi. Recently, they were supposed to accept the provincial government's unconditional disbandment order, but were coerced by their subordinates and rebelled. Wang's father lives in Yutian City and has sent a letter urging his son to return quickly. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) On the afternoon of the 28th, Han Dianbang, the captain of the Yutian Security Corps, came to the province and immediately visited Yu Xuezhong at the provincial government to report on the reorganization of the security corps and request instructions on the second phase of downsizing. Long-distance telephones have been installed throughout Fengrun County to facilitate the communication of news from various towns. The authorities plan to hold a county-wide event there and then continue in other counties. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) After the aborted Yutian militia mutiny, Yin Rugeng telegraphed Wei Yonghe, the captain of the security corps, from Tianjin, urging him to rush to Jixian to meet with Li Chao, the magistrate of Zunhua County, Chen Baosheng, the magistrate of Yutian County, and Wu Minghao, the magistrate of Jixian County, to go to Shimentown to summon Wang Bingkao and the militia captains to guide and persuade them. On the morning of the 28th, Wei arrived at Shimentown with the three magistrates and Li Weizhou, the leader of the Jixian militia, and invited Wang and the unit captains Zhao Wenyuan and Zhao Jingqi to talk. At that time, the unit had retreated to Mashen Bridge. Due to the unfavorable situation, more than a hundred people automatically dispersed. Wang has softened as a result and is expected to comply with the order for a peaceful resolution. The specific plan is still under negotiation and is expected to be decided on the evening of the 28th. Yin telegraphed the political and military councils separately on the 28th to report on the progress. (Special dispatch, 28th)

The Lu and Liu Brigades will each have a strength of 5,000 men. The orders appointing the brigade commanders have been issued. 23

(Beiping) The sub-committee has issued an order appointing Lu Fengnian as the lieutenant general brigade commander of the 117th Brigade of the Army Infantry and Liu Yueting as the lieutenant general brigade commander of the 118th Brigade of the Army Infantry. The seals and appointment certificates were delivered by the sixth group of the sub-committee on the 28th. It has been decided that the Lu and Liu brigades will each have a strength of 5,000 men. Their uniforms and living allowance funds can be claimed immediately and remitted. The uniforms will be changed after the unit arrives at the Xizhimen Station. Lu has telegraphed Bao Ling to send the special duty regiment first. Lu and Liu will return to Bao after the troops move to settle everything. Yu Shiming is scheduled to go to Xuchang on the 30th or 1st because all of his cavalry has passed through Ping. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Beiping) Over a thousand soldiers and family members of Sun's unit arrived in Ping on the 28th. The Ministry of Finance Reorganizes Land Tax and Plans to Establish Standards for Handling Local Budgets 29

(Nanjing) In order to reorganize the land tax, the Ministry of Finance has formulated five standards for reorganizing local budgets and has sent them to the provincial governments for their information and compliance. Briefly, it states that in times of peace, taxes are lightly levied, but in times of chaos, taxes and levies are necessarily heavy. In the late stages of each dynasty, exploitation and oppression were rampant, leading to inevitable cycles of cause and effect and ruin. After the establishment of the Republic of China, military figures were autocratic, and internal strife was frequent. The people suffered from banditry and were also burdened by official rent. Working hard throughout the year was not enough to pay taxes. The Fourth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang passed two proposals to reorganize the land tax, conduct land reporting, and reduce land tax surcharges to relieve the rural areas. These proposals aimed to clarify the tax amount, determine property rights, strictly eliminate abuses, and equalize the burden. As for land tax surcharges, they should be substantially reduced. As for county local budgets, they should be accurately verified. Miscellaneous taxes and levies have been repeatedly abolished by the Executive Yuan's order, but local revenues are often increased due to new policies or temporary anti-banditry efforts. Once they are added, they become the norm, accumulating endlessly. In some cases, land tax surcharges exceed several times the amount of the original tax. The root cause of the problem is that there is no definite budget for the locality. Now, if we want to reduce and fix the amount of taxes, we should first start by determining the local budget. Attached are five standards for handling local budgets: 1. Reorganize local finances and live within one's means, not the other way around, so as not to resort to excessive taxation. 2. Local administrative affairs must be considered in order of urgency and extravagance should be eliminated to ensure that income and expenditure are in balance. 3. The budget for the 23rd year must be prepared urgently. The ministry convened a financial conference to discuss the local finances and determine the budget. Local governments should make real cuts within the scope of not affecting necessary affairs, and compile a general budget and submit it for approval. 4. If there is any extravagance in the budget compiled by the counties, it should be strictly rejected. 5. After the budget is determined, if there is a surplus in the counties, it should be turned over to the provincial government. If the province has a surplus, it should be reported to the central government for approval and accumulated for local construction in the province. The county budget will be approved by the province, and if there is a shortfall, the province will find ways to subsidize it from the provincial treasury. The provincial budget will be approved by the central government, and if there is a shortfall, the central government will find ways to subsidize it. It is requested that you investigate, forward these to those who need to know, and earnestly comply with them, and also hope to see a reply. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Jiang Orders Five Provinces to Ban Labor Unions from Collecting Membership Fees and Sets Working Hours at Ten Hours 32

(Nanchang) Chairman Jiang recently issued a telegram to the chairmen and party headquarters of the five provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian in order to reduce the burden on workers and accelerate production efficiency. The original telegram stated: Eliminating labor unrest and stabilizing society is currently the most crucial plan for the bandit suppression provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian. The primary cause of previous labor unrest has been demands for increased wages. Therefore, reducing the economic suffering of workers is the most effective way to eliminate labor unrest. The factory labor unions constantly collect membership fees or other fees from workers, causing the income earned by workers through their blood and sweat to be subjected to unnecessary exploitation. Although Article 17 of the Labor Union Law stipulates that labor unions may collect membership fees, regular fees, special funds, temporary fundraising, or shares from workers, this is a peacetime regulation. Under the special circumstances of the bandit suppression period in the five provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian, such regulations cannot be applied without modification in order to avoid interfering with the bandit suppression work and adapt to the current environment. All provisions of Article 17 of the Labor Union Law should be temporarily suspended in the five bandit suppression provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian. In the future, factory labor unions will not be allowed to collect membership fees or any other fees from workers. It must be understood that reducing the expenditure of workers is no different from increasing their income. This should be strictly prohibited, and the handling should be reported for review. Furthermore, eight hours of work is the general practice in various countries, but the main purpose of its legislation is to curb overproduction. China's production industry is already backward and does not suffer from overproduction but rather from insufficiency. To curb overproduction in an insufficient country is a misguided policy. Moreover, the five provinces of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian have been affected by banditry for many years, and their production has declined even more than before. It will not be easy to restore vitality without striving to accelerate production. Although Article 8 of the revised Factory Law also stipulates that the actual working hours for adult workers each day should be eight hours in principle, there is a provision that allows for extending the hours to ten if the local situation or the nature of the work requires it. Therefore, under the special circumstances of the above five provinces, this provision should be appropriately applied to promote increased production. In the future, the daily working hours of workers in all factories, except for child laborers, should be set at ten hours as the standard, so that work that takes workers in other countries five days to complete can be completed by workers in our country in just four days. What is insufficient on a daily basis will be more than enough on a monthly or annual basis. The increased effort of one person is not obvious, but the combined increased effort of workers in several provinces will be enormous. By catching up quickly in this way, the contribution to the enrichment of national power and the restoration of local vitality will be significant. It is hoped that you will forward this telegram for compliance, pay close attention to the matter, and not allow factory owners to mistreat workers. If there is mistreatment, workers in that area can truthfully report to the local officials of the province, who will forward it to this headquarters for impartial handling, without any favoritism. Labor and management should each be treated fairly and live in peace, so that they can jointly overcome the economic crisis of the country. In addition to sending separate telegrams and orders, this telegram is specifically issued for compliance, and it is hoped that the telegram will be copied and posted at the entrances of all labor unions and factories for everyone to observe. Jiang Zhongzheng (You). (Central News Agency dispatch, 27th)

The Kalachakra Dharma Assembly is Inaugurated; the Panchen Lama Presides over the Chanting of Sutras 39

(Hangzhou) The Kalachakra Dharma Assembly, presided over by the Panchen Lama, began construction at Lingyin Temple at 9:00 AM on the 28th. Before 9:00 AM, Zhang Zaiyang, Zhao Yanwu, Wang Yiting, and other directors of the association, as well as more than 200 monks from Lingyin Temple, held incense and formed a procession to welcome the Panchen Lama at Zhu Zhuang. The Panchen Lama then brought a small black foreign dog and rode in a yellow sedan chair to Lingyin Temple to begin presiding over the chanting of sutras. The ceremonies were similar to welcoming a deity. The congestion of the audience and those kneeling in prayer caused the clay Bodhisattvas to pale in comparison. A reporter from the Central News Agency made a special visit to the Panchen Lama at his residence at 8:00 AM on the 28th. Through his secretary-general, Liu Jiaju, as a translator, the Panchen Lama said that this was his second visit to Hangzhou and that he would stay in Hangzhou for three weeks. Regarding the issue of returning to Tibet, he said that he would have to attend the Dharma assembly and would temporarily ask Secretary-General Liu to convey his views. At that time, those welcoming the Panchen Lama to the Dharma assembly were already lined up and waiting respectfully outside the mansion and sent several representatives to prostrate themselves before him. The reporter then took his leave. Later, according to Liu Jiaju, the Panchen Lama's return to Tibet was only a matter of time. When the Dalai Lama was dying, he had already expressed his sincerity in welcoming the Panchen Lama to Anqin Hutuktu and other representatives of the Panchen Lama who went to Tibet. At present, the authorities and people of both the front and rear Tibet are unanimously and enthusiastically welcoming the Panchen Lama. The chairman of the front Tibet government and religion, Silon Kasha, recently sent a telegram from Calcutta urging the Panchen Lama to return to Tibet. Moreover, the rear Tibet has now sent 56 representatives of all the monks and laity, including Ding Jieke Tu, to Beijing to urge his return. However, because the certification letters and other documents were still on the way, they had not yet formally met with the Panchen Lama. It is expected that Anqin and others will accompany them to Hangzhou to meet the Panchen Lama within a few days. At that time, the Panchen Lama will have a formal statement on the issue of returning to Tibet. As for when he will set off, he will listen to the orders of the central government. As for the original purpose of the Panchen Lama's return to Tibet, it is entirely to seek coordination between the central government and Tibet, not for personal power and position. In addition, Chairman Lin specially sent Xie Jian to Hangzhou to present the Panchen Lama with a white jade incense burner and several pieces of Magu as souvenirs and to express his condolences. Furthermore, the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly is scheduled to end on the 13th of next month. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

German Foreign Minister Neurath Severely Criticizes France for Undermining Disarmament and Expanding Armaments, Wanting to Force Others to Relieve Political Injustice, Nothing Could Be More Excessive 45

(Berlin) Today, German Foreign Minister Neurath met with German journalists and issued the following statement on the issue of disarmament:

Negotiations on the disarmament conference have been underway for more than six months, but today France has abruptly undermined them. There is no need to refute the attacks and insults against Germany in the French memorandum, and France's other real intentions are also very clear. The figures in the German budget used for national defense are not its true target of attack. France has spent a huge sum of 1.6 billion francs on expanding its military preparations in the past year, and now it is surprised by its neighbor's military expenditure of 18 million marks, which is truly incomprehensible. Moreover, Germany has fully complied with its obligations regarding disarmament, but the other party's actions, namely the universal reduction of armaments by other countries, have not yet begun, and in fact, they have been delayed for several years, and today there is still no sign of implementation. The continued existence of such a state of affairs, such as Germany's unilateral disarmament while other countries' armaments are expanding to an unprecedented degree, or are still in the process of expansion, is absolutely unfair and politically impossible. If we want to judge this state of affairs based on fundamental legal principles today, we must first answer the following questions: Who is right and who is wrong between Germany and France? Should France insist on the reasons for its last memorandum, or should Germany demand equality of status and equal armaments with other countries, especially as sufficient as France? We are still willing to reach a peaceful understanding with France today, so we have sent a special representative for disarmament, granting him full authority to allow international negotiations to proceed smoothly. But today, we understand the dangers ahead, all of which are caused by France's actions. We only know that our viewpoint is flawless in law, morality, and politics, and we can wait for future changes without any doubts. (27th National Telegram)

Davis recently took leave to return to the U.S. and will soon return to Europe to participate in the Geneva Conference on May 23 as an unofficial representative. Davis did not participate in the discussions; his only task was to report important news to Washington. It is understood that Davis told the President that there is no hope for an early completion of disarmament, and the situation will become clearer in a month. Government policy has not changed. In his special message to Congress on January 3, President Roosevelt declared that the United States could not participate in European political problems but was willing to cooperate with Europe to complete any plan to reduce armaments or commercial barriers. Disarmament talks have now effectively stalled because France recently stated in its note that it cannot agree to disarmament because Germany is currently spending more money to rebuild its armaments. Britain still believes that the Geneva Disarmament Conference will achieve some concrete results. Disarmament talks have been underway for six months, and Britain has abandoned its hope of concluding a preliminary agreement with France, Italy, and Germany. (27th National News Agency Dispatch)

Meeting of German Creditor Groups: Britain and France Issue Serious Warnings Against Germany Suspending Indemnity Payments 49

(Berlin) France is following in Britain's footsteps today, with its ambassador to Germany informing the German government that France will take any proposal to suspend the remittance of Dawes and Young loans very seriously. In other words, France, like Britain, hopes that German indemnity payments will continue to be remitted. However, Hjalmar Schacht of the Deutsche Bank has stated that Germany can no longer raise the necessary annual debt repayment of £23 million. German creditors are also meeting at the Deutsche Bank today to discuss the remittance issue.

Although their deliberations do not technically include Dawes and Young bonds, their resolutions will inevitably affect them. There is no doubt about this. The meeting will be divided into two subcommittees, which will continue to discuss tomorrow. Participants seem determined to oppose the complete suspension of remittances of over £10 million in 7% Dawes loans issued in 1924 and 5.5% Young loans issued in 1920. Britain supplied approximately £24 million for both loans, which are Germany's direct and unconditional obligations. The warnings from the British and French governments have caused great panic in financial circles. Secondly, the German creditors' meeting has opened in a completely new atmosphere, and its duration seems to be very short. German creditors feel that Dawes and Young loans cannot be made an exception, as this would harm a large group of German private creditors. Private creditors intend to clearly state that Germany must take concrete steps to create a more sympathetic atmosphere overseas, so that German goods can sell well. It has been said that Germany's inability to repay its debts is due to obstacles to its export trade. (27th Reuters Dispatch)

The Italian government is now striving to increase the efficiency of the Italian army, but this relies on the construction of the legion as the basis, so that it can be expanded when needed, and on the unity of military power. Now it is necessary to strive to improve the physique of Italian youth and their military training, so as to raise the standard of military efficiency. It is important to renovate war equipment and unify military power. Italy, with its new political system as a guide for other countries, should be able to promote the revision of the constitutional government of other countries. Italy is eager to assist in solving important issues in Europe and the world and is determined to maintain good relations with the Holy See. The Italian King ended by mentioning the need for a balanced budget and reiterating the Italian government's view of maintaining the gold standard. Bombay Labor Strike Spreads; Number of Workers Reaches 65,000 55

Bombay The labor strike at 40 yarn factories in Bombay has spread, with the number of strikers reaching 65,000. Today, clashes occurred twice between strikers and non-strikers. When the strikers attacked the non-strikers, the police were forced to open fire. Although several people were injured, the rioters did not disperse. The crowd threw stones at the police, injuring many police officers. The area where the incident occurred is now heavily guarded. (27th Reuters Dispatch)

Islamic Countries Clash; Hejaz Troops Win Repeated Victories 56

(London) King Ibn Saud of the Arab Hejaz and Imam Yahya of Yemen failed to reach a settlement in July due to a misunderstanding, so they went to war in mid-March. According to news from London, the Hejaz troops have won repeated victories. Recently, they pursued the defeated army in the Al-Arashi area with armored vehicles, captured the commander of the Yemeni army, and it is reported that they have occupied the town of Midi. Yemen is an independent country on the southern coast of Arabia and, like the Hejaz, adheres to Islam. (28th Reuters Dispatch)

Special Reuters Wire Service Telegram, April 28— 60

Gold and Silver: The London gold price today was 135 shillings and 9 pence, down 2 pence from yesterday.

London Silver: The London silver market was stable today. The spot price was 19 pence 0.625, and the futures price was 19 pence 1.25, both up 3.125. The Bank of China made purchases in the morning, and sellers were scarce, so the price rose. After the price rose, China sold, and the market situation at the close was uncertain.

New York Silver: The silver market opened firm due to favorable foreign news, and it was heard that President Roosevelt had stated to members of Congress that he could support silver as 30% of the currency reserves. There was some profit-taking when the price rose, but the sentiment was optimistic because the profit-taking of the bulls gradually stopped. The market situation later turned quiet, but the actual position was more stable, and President Roosevelt's moderate tone made the market situation still stable. The forward opening price was 5 to 0 points higher than yesterday's closing price.

Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market was stable today. The spot price was 52 rupees and 13 annas, up 10 annas. The May futures price was up 9 annas, and the June futures price was up 8 annas.

Exchange Rates 61

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was sluggish this morning. The opening price for the British-American exchange rate was 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 4 and a half cents, up 125 from yesterday's American-British exchange rate closing price. At 11 o'clock, the price remained unchanged. At noon, it fell by 125 to 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 4.375 cents, but at the close, it returned to 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 4.4375 cents, 0.0625 lower than this morning's opening price. Also, 1 U.S. dollar equals 3 shillings and 653 British pounds.

British-French: The opening price was 77 francs 34, the same as yesterday's closing price. At 11 o'clock, it rose 6 points to 77 francs 40, and there was no change until the close.

American-British: The New York exchange rate for British pounds opened today at 5.14.25, the same as the second offer, slightly lower 125 than the previous day's close. The third and fourth offers changed to 5.14.875, and the sixth offer was 5.15.125.

American-French: The New York exchange rate for French francs opened today at 6.65.00

Cotton and Wheat 62

American Cotton: The cotton market was stable due to demand from traders, purchases from foreign Liverpool and Europe, and the short side covering positions. The selling by retail New Orleans and spot merchants was absorbed. Although brokers expected the price to continue to rise, the market situation rebounded due to profit-taking. The buying appetite was not strong, and merchants are now awaiting developments.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was more stable today. The July futures price was 5.72, up 4 points.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market's July futures price this morning was 4 shillings and 4 and 125 pence, up 375.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market rose today following news from New York, but later fell due to profit-taking and bull liquidations. The July-August Bailuozhi cotton futures price was 190 rupees, up half a rupee.

Rubber 63

The New York market was quite stable because London was strong and the restriction measures were expected to be announced soon. Speculators made some purchases, but they were half offset by profit-taking.

The London rubber market was firm this morning. At the close, the trading price for July and September futures was 6 pence and 7 thirty-seconds, the same as yesterday's price.

Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to Raise Funds to Repay China-British Bank Loan 66

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Railways, the 31st installment of the principal of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway's debt to the China-British Bank, plus bank expenses, totaling £37,593 and 15 shillings, has already been partially repaid in February with £19,500. Now, the remaining £8,093 and 15 shillings, plus a portion of the 32nd installment of the principal, totaling £406 and 5 shillings, are combined to raise £18,500 to be repaid together. In addition to 100,000 yuan allocated by the ministry, the remainder will be paid from the special reserve fund. The railway's accounting office has now determined the exchange rate, equivalent to 277,230 yuan, and on April 20, a check was issued and delivered to HSBC for remittance to London. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) Weng Wenhao, accompanied by his wife and Guan Songtao, a brain specialist from Peking Union Medical College Hospital, arrived in Nanjing on the evening of the 27th and went directly to Zhongshan Hospital for rest. On the morning of the 28th, Qian Changzhao and his wife, along with Supervisor Gao Lu and University President Luo Jialun, visited him at the hospital. Director Wang also inquired about Weng’s condition by telephone. At 5 p.m. on the 28th, Weng, accompanied by his wife and Dr. Guan, crossed the river to Pukou in a Central Hospital ambulance and took the Pingpu train north at 7 p.m., arriving in Beiping on the morning of the 30th. According to those close to Weng, his wounds have healed, but his vitality has not yet recovered and he still needs long-term convalescence. Weng is now completely conscious, and his pulse and temperature are normal. Only his left forehead is slightly sunken, and there is still a piece of fragmented bone and a blood clot in his brain. Whether this will cause significant damage to the brain remains to be determined after a stereoscopic X-ray examination at Peking Union Medical College Hospital in Beiping. If it is indeed harmful, surgery will be performed to remove it. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)
